    </p><div id="art-admin"><span class="italic bold">Received 
      17th April 2023
    </span><span class="bold italic">, Accepted 26th June 2023</span></div><p class="bold italic">First published on 30th June 2023</p><hr><div class="abstract"><h2>Abstract</h2><p>Sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) display the essential properties required of a reliable energy-storage device, such as vast availability, good voltage output, and cost-effectiveness. Although initial SIB cathodes delivered a significantly lower capacity than their lithium-ion battery counterparts, new high-capacity cathode materials for SIBs continue to be developed today. This study employed a combined machine-learning (ML), <span class="italic">ab initio</span> density functional theory (DFT), and experimental approach to develop low-cost and high-energy cathode materials, <span class="italic">i.e.</span> Na<small><sub>3.5</sub></small>MnV<small><sub>0.5</sub></small>Ti<small><sub>0.5</sub></small>(PO<small><sub>4</sub></small>)<small><sub>3</sub></small> (NMVTP), Na<small><sub>3.5</sub></small>MnV<small><sub>0.5</sub></small>Fe<small><sub>0.5</sub></small>(PO<small><sub>4</sub></small>)<small><sub>3</sub></small> (NMVFP), and Na<small><sub>3.5</sub></small>MnV<small><sub>0.5</sub></small>Al<small><sub>0.5</sub></small>(PO<small><sub>4</sub></small>)<small><sub>3</sub></small> (NMVAP). Among these materials, the carbon-coated Na<small><sub>3.5</sub></small>MnV<small><sub>0.5</sub></small>Ti<small><sub>0.5</sub></small>(PO<small><sub>4</sub></small>)<small><sub>3</sub></small> (NMVTP/C) with the most stable formation energy (1.99 eV) registered an exceedingly high specific capacity of 133.14 mA h g<small><sup>1</sup></small>, a satisfactory Na<small><sup>+</sup></small> (de)insertion voltage of 3.42 V, and a superior energy output of 455 W h kg<small><sup>1</sup></small> in the half-cell configuration. NMVTP/C also exhibits a rapid sodium storage capability for 8000 cycles with a capacity retention of 75% at a considerably high current rate of 14C and an impressive rate proficiency of 59.2 mA h g<small><sup>1</sup></small> at 17.5C.</p></div><hr>
    
      
      <h2 id="sect348"><span class="a_heading">1. Introduction</span></h2>
      <span>Sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) are one of the most studied energy-storage devices at present, after lithium-ion batteries (LIBs).<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit1"><sup><span class="sup_ref">1</span></sup></a> SIBs were first introduced for electronic devices in the 1980s.<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit2"><sup><span class="sup_ref">2</span></sup></a> However, the successful commercialization of LIBs in the earlier part of the decade, owing to their high performance, stagnated the development of SIBs.<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit3"><sup><span class="sup_ref">3</span></sup></a> Nevertheless, research on SIBs considerably accelerated in the 21st century when researchers realized the inability of the available lithium resources to meet the increasing demands for LIBs, especially for grid-scale requirements.<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit4"><sup><span class="sup_ref">4</span></sup></a> SIBs made their entry into electronics initially as a potential substitute to LIBs because of the low cost and vast availability of sodium resources. However, they remained significantly inferior to the well-established LIBs in terms of working voltage, specific energy, and electrochemical stability.<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit5"><sup><span class="sup_ref">5</span></sup></a> Researchers have undertaken extensive efforts to develop suitable cathode materials for SIBs, including olivines,<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit6"><sup><span class="sup_ref">6</span></sup></a> sodium super-ionic conductor (NASICON) structures,<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit7"><sup><span class="sup_ref">7</span></sup></a> Prussian blue compounds,<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit8"><sup><span class="sup_ref">8</span></sup></a> mixed-polyanion materials,<a title="Select to navigate to reference" href="#cit9"><sup><span class="sup_ref">9,10</span></sup></a> and layered oxides,<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit11"><sup><span class="sup_ref">11</span></sup></a> to resolve the above-mentioned issues.<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit12"><sup><span class="sup_ref">12</span></sup></a></span>
      <p class="otherpara">Among the electrode materials established for SIBs, phosphates with a NASICON structure are promising because of their balanced crystallographic structure; this could facilitate reliable sodium storage properties. The most explored cathode material from the NASICON family is Na<small><sub>3</sub></small>V<small><sub>2</sub></small>(PO<small><sub>4</sub></small>)<small><sub>3</sub></small> (NVP), which has a high theoretical capacity of 110 mA h g<small><sup>1</sup></small> and a working potential of 3.33.4 V.<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit13"><sup><span class="sup_ref">13</span></sup></a> Although NVP is an ideal cathode for SIBs, its inclusion of the expensive and harmful V element restricts its wide-range utilization.<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit14"><sup><span class="sup_ref">14</span></sup></a> To overcome this issue, Goodenough's group substituted the V element in the structure with eco-friendly transition metal ions.<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit15"><sup><span class="sup_ref">15</span></sup></a> Owing to the systematic and decisive efforts of various research groups, multiple NASICON-type cathodes for SIBs have been successfully fabricated through cation swapping, including Na<small><sub>3</sub></small>MnTi(PO<small><sub>4</sub></small>)<small><sub>3</sub></small>, Na<small><sub>4</sub></small>MnV(PO<small><sub>4</sub></small>)<small><sub>3</sub></small>, Na<small><sub>3</sub></small>FeV(PO<small><sub>4</sub></small>)<small><sub>3</sub></small>, Na<small><sub>3</sub></small>MnZr(PO<small><sub>4</sub></small>)<small><sub>3</sub></small>, Na<small><sub>3.5</sub></small>Mn<small><sub>0.5</sub></small>V<small><sub>1.5</sub></small>(PO<small><sub>4</sub></small>)<small><sub>3,</sub></small> and Na<small><sub>2</sub></small>VTi(PO<small><sub>4</sub></small>)<small><sub>3</sub></small>.<a title="Select to navigate to reference" href="#cit7"><sup><span class="sup_ref">7,1417</span></sup></a> However, these cathode materials remain insufficient in terms of capacity and average working potential for large-scale energy-storage devices.<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit18"><sup><span class="sup_ref">18</span></sup></a> First-principles calculations based on density functional theory (DFT) and machine-learning (ML) have emerged as potential tools to accelerate materials discovery. Compared to the common way of finding potential candidates by trial-error, DFT and ML approaches were found to be effective and time-efficient.<a title="Select to navigate to reference" href="#cit19"><sup><span class="sup_ref">1921</span></sup></a> DFT method reformulates the Schrodinger equation of ground-state energy to the electron density by implementing several approximations. With the DFT method, material properties can be predicted, including physical, chemical, and electrical properties.<a title="Select to navigate to reference" href="#cit22"><sup><span class="sup_ref">2224</span></sup></a> In the case of ML, the computer, without explicitly being programmed, learns the pattern that exists in the dataset, and with the help of algorithms, it can derive the relationship in the data and predict the target output, and in this case, material properties. Therefore, the ML technique can also be a very powerful screening tool for materials selection in a short period of time.<a title="Select to navigate to reference" href="#cit25"><sup><span class="sup_ref">2527</span></sup></a> In addition, a combined ML-DFT method has also been demonstrated to predict several properties and led to the discovery of extraordinary materials.<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit25"><sup><span class="sup_ref">25</span></sup></a> In light of the above discussion, we present a practical ML-DFT-experiment procedure for seeking new cathode materials for SIBs. We first used the ML technique to predict the crystal stability of the proposed electrode materials. Crystal stability is an important factor in the search for new materials.<a title="Select to navigate to reference" href="#cit28"><sup><span class="sup_ref">28,29</span></sup></a> Subsequently, we used DFT to validate these structures.</p>
      <p class="otherpara">Using ML and DFT methods, we proposed formerly-unexplored cathodes, <span class="italic">i.e.</span> Na<small><sub>3.5</sub></small>MnV<small><sub>0.5</sub></small>Ti<small><sub>0.5</sub></small>(PO<small><sub>4</sub></small>)<small><sub>3</sub></small> (NMVTP), Na<small><sub>3.5</sub></small>MnV<small><sub>0.5</sub></small>Fe<small><sub>0.5</sub></small>(PO<small><sub>4</sub></small>)<small><sub>3</sub></small> (NMVFP), and Na<small><sub>3.5</sub></small>MnV<small><sub>0.5</sub></small>Al<small><sub>0.5</sub></small>(PO<small><sub>4</sub></small>)<small><sub>3</sub></small> (NMVAP). We then attempted to synthesize these compounds and characterize the electrochemical properties for SIB applications. Furthermore, to verify the predicted structures the proposed cathodes are prepared using rapid pyro-synthesis techniques, and their electrochemical properties are comprehensively investigated. When defended as a cathode for SIBs, NMVTP/C exhibits superior electrochemical properties. In particular, the as-designed uniformly carbon-shielded NMVTP/C microflakes displayed a commendable reversible capacity of 133.14 mA h g<small><sup>1</sup></small> at 0.17C, a satisfactory average discharge potential of V, and superior specific energy of 455 W h kg<small><sup>1</sup></small>. The presence of Mn, Ti, and V not only preserves the crystal structure, but also boosts the practical capacity and functioning voltage of the cathode <span class="italic">via</span> multiple (V<small><sup>2+/3+</sup></small>, Ti<small><sup>3+/4+</sup></small>, V<small><sup>3+/4+</sup></small>, Mn<small><sup>2+/3+</sup></small>, and V<small><sup>4+/5+</sup></small>) redox couples. <span class="italic">In situ</span> X-ray diffraction (XRD) and galvanostatic intermittent titration technique (GITT) studies demonstrate the integrated single-phase and two-phase reversible Na<small><sup>+</sup></small> (de)insertion properties of the NMVTP/C cathode during the electrochemical charge/discharge process.</p>
    
    
      
      <h2 id="sect426"><span class="a_heading">2. Results and discussion</span></h2>
      <span>In the search for new electrode materials for SIB application, our proposed platform consists of three parts, <span class="italic">i.e.</span>, ML model-prediction, DFT calculations, and experimental validation (<a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig1">Fig. 1a</a>). Here we first predicted the crystal stability of the proposed structure using the ML model. The available dataset of formation energy per atom for ML was retrieved from the Materials Project (MP).<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit30"><sup><span class="sup_ref">30</span></sup></a> DFT calculations were then used to optimize the proposed structures and finally, we attempted to synthesize the selected material and thoroughly characterize it. From the MP database, we were able to obtain 35<img class="charmap" src="https://www.rsc.org/images/entities/char_2009.gif" alt="[thin space (1/6-em)]">209 entries. After data cleansing by removing the duplicates, we finally had 24<img class="charmap" src="https://www.rsc.org/images/entities/char_2009.gif" alt="[thin space (1/6-em)]">695 data. 176 descriptors from Matminer were used for data featurization. 4 algorithms were used for training the ML models, <span class="italic">i.e.</span> XG Boost (XGB) from University of Washington, Random Forest (RF), Bayesian Ridge (BR), and Support Vector Machine (SVM) Regressions from Scikit-Learn.<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit31"><sup><span class="sup_ref">31</span></sup></a> These ML models were selected due to several considerations. With current dataset and numerous descriptors, XG Boost can effectively learn complex relationships and interactions among the features. Random Forest can exploit the diversity of decision trees to capture complex patterns and provide robust predictions. Bayesian Ridge and Support Vector Machine Regressions are effective in high-dimensional spaces and can capture complex patterns in the data. Furthermore, SVM model has the ability to find optimal hyperplanes to separate data points. Other algorithms such as Neural networks (NNs), Expectation Maximization (EM), Adaboost, k-Nearest Neighbors (kNN), and decision trees are also powerful to capture complex relationships within materials elements.<a title="Select to navigate to reference" href="#cit32"><sup><span class="sup_ref">3234</span></sup></a> However, for example, NNs often require huge amounts of data for training, and also training deep neural networks can be computationally expensive. It is worth considering that if computational resources were limited, it might have been challenging to train and optimize neural networks effectively. kNN might face challenges when dealing with high-dimensional datasets (176 descriptors). kNN tends to perform better with larger datasets, and with 24<img class="charmap" src="https://www.rsc.org/images/entities/char_2009.gif" alt="[thin space (1/6-em)]">695 data points, the performance might not be optimal compared to other algorithms that are specifically designed for high-dimensional data, such as XG Boost and Random Forest. Indeed, this requires further studies and exceeds the boundaries of our present study. The effectivity of ML models was then assessed using the coefficient of determination (<span class="italic">R</span><small><sup>2</sup></small>), and root mean square error (RMSE). Fig. S1 (ESI<a title="Select to navigate to footnote" href="#fn1"></a>) depicts the test results of each ML model. The SVM Regression shows better performance than XGB, RF, and BR with <span class="italic">R</span><small><sup>2</sup></small> and RMSE values of 0.927 and 0.25, respectively. The <span class="italic">R</span><small><sup>2</sup></small> value above 0.9 can be an indication of a good model, particularly for predicting formation energy.<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit21"><sup><span class="sup_ref">21</span></sup></a> Further optimization of the SVM algorithm was performed using GridSearchCV (Fig. S2<a title="Select to navigate to footnote" href="#fn1"></a>).</span>
      <br><div class="image_table"><table><tbody><tr><td colspan="3" class="imgHolder" id="imgfig1"><a href="/image/article/2023/TA/d3ta02291a/d3ta02291a-f1_hi-res.gif" title="Select to open image in new window" onclick="open(this.href, &quot;_blank&quot;, &quot;toolbar=1,scrollbars=yes,resizable=1&quot;); return false;"><img alt="image file: d3ta02291a-f1.tif" src="/image/article/2023/TA/d3ta02291a/d3ta02291a-f1.gif"></a></td></tr><tr><td class="pushTitleRight"> </td><td class="image_title"><b>Fig. 1 </b> <span id="fig1"><span class="graphic_title">(a) Schematic illustration of cathode material formulation for SIBs <span class="italic">via</span> combined ML-DFT and experimental model. (b) Scatter plot showing predicted formation energy <span class="italic">vs.</span> DFT formation energy with different algorithms used in this work. (c) XRD Rietveld refinement pattern for NMVTP (inset goodness-of-fit value). (d) Crystal structure model of NMVTP. HRTEM images of NMVTP/C containing (e) low magnifications. (f) Carbon-coating. (g) Interplanar <span class="italic">d</span>-spacing and (h) elemental mapping in bright field image with corresponding elements (Na, Mn, V, Ti, P, O, C).</span></span></td><td class="pushTitleLeft"> </td></tr></tbody></table></div>
      <p class="otherpara">The optimized C and gamma values were found to be 1000 and 0.1, respectively. After implementing the optimized C and gamma values in the SVM Regression model, the test result was improved with <span class="italic">R</span><small><sup>2</sup></small> and RMSE values of 0.944 and 0.22, respectively (<a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig1">Fig. 1b</a>). Accordingly, we selected the SVM model for crystal stability prediction of new proposed SIB cathode materials. Since we focus on the NASICON-derived compounds; we thus proposed and predicted 3 new compounds, <span class="italic">i.e.</span>, NMVTP, NMVFP, and NMVAP. The choice of different elements for replacing vanadium in Na<small><sub>3.5</sub></small>V<small><sub>2</sub></small>(PO<small><sub>4</sub></small>)<small><sub>3</sub></small>, such as manganese, titanium, iron, and aluminum, were basically also based on several scientific considerations such as chemical similarity, ionic radii, availability and cost, and desired properties.<a title="Select to navigate to reference" href="#cit35"><sup><span class="sup_ref">35,36</span></sup></a> Manganese, titanium, iron, and aluminum are all transition metals like vanadium and share some similarities in terms of electronic structure and bonding. From structural perspective, it is important to consider elements with similar ionic radii to minimize structural distortion. The ionic radii of those ions, <span class="italic">i.e.</span> Mn<small><sup>2+</sup></small>, Ti<small><sup>4+</sup></small>, Fe<small><sup>2+</sup></small>, and Al<small><sup>3+</sup></small> are reasonably close to that of V<small><sup>5+</sup></small>, which may allow high possibility for successful substitution. Indeed, for practical considerations such as the availability and cost of the replacement elements also play a role in material selection. Manganese, titanium, iron, and aluminum are relatively abundant and widely used in various industries, which makes them more accessible and cost-effective compared to some other elements including vanadium. Overall, each element substitution can potentially influence properties such as ionic conductivity, thermal stability, electrochemical performance, and structural stability. By using the ML model, the predicted formation energy per atom of NMVTP, NMVFP, and NMVAP were 1.99, 1.86, and 1.82 eV, respectively. The results indicate that the proposed compounds are predicted to possess good crystal stability with NMVTP being the most stable. We then turn to DFT calculations to validate the proposed structures. The relaxed structures of the proposed compounds are depicted in <a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig1">Fig. 1d</a> and S3.<a title="Select to navigate to footnote" href="#fn1"></a> The lattice parameters of these structures are also presented in Table. S1.<a title="Select to navigate to footnote" href="#fn1"></a> It can be observed that all the structures were able to preserve the NASICON characteristics. However, NMVAP experienced more distortion and exhibited relatively narrower unit cells compared to these of NMVTP and NMVFP. Previous reports indicate that a slightly larger channel in the structure is preferable for SIB applications.<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit37"><sup><span class="sup_ref">37</span></sup></a> Furthermore, to verify the proposed observation the corresponding structures (NMVAP, NMVFP, and NMVTP) were further subjected to synthesis and characterization. It is expected that the proposed structure is promising for the SIB system.</p>
      <p class="otherpara">Firstly, to verify the electrochemical sodium storage properties of the ML-DFT predicted (NMVAP, NMVFP, and NMVTP) materials were synthesized <span class="italic">via</span> a rapid pyro-synthesis process (the detailed information can be found in the ESI<a title="Select to navigate to footnote" href="#fn1"></a>). The crystal features of the prepared cathode materials were analyzed using the PXRD, and the results are provided in Fig. S4.<a title="Select to navigate to footnote" href="#fn1"></a> It can be witnessed that the carbon-coated NMVAP/C, NMVFP/C, and NMVTP/C samples crystallize in the NASICON structured phase of trigonal symmetry with a space group of <span class="italic">R</span><img class="charmap" src="https://www.rsc.org/images/entities/char_0033_0304.gif" alt="[3 with combining macron]"><span class="italic">c</span>. Though, the NMVFP/C belongs to the NASICON family additional phase is evidenced, indicating the existence of pyrophosphates during the annealing. Since the NMVTP/C sample exhibited estimable electrochemical Na<small><sup>+</sup></small> storage properties, we have adopted Rietveld refinement (using X'Pert Highscore Plus Program) to determine the crystal structure of the NMVTP/C cathode. The Bragg diffractions peak at (012), (104), (113), (006), (024), (211), (122), (030), (220), (131), (134), (042), (404), (232), (140), (143), (502), and (330), as shown in <a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig1">Fig. 1c</a>, are indexed well to a trigonal symmetry with a space group of <span class="italic">R</span><img class="charmap" src="https://www.rsc.org/images/entities/char_0033_0304.gif" alt="[3 with combining macron]"><span class="italic">c</span>, according to X'pert Highscore software. The results of the structural framework of the Rietveld refinement are presented in Table S2.<a title="Select to navigate to footnote" href="#fn1"></a> From the structural refinement, the lattice parameters of NMVTP were calculated to be <span class="italic">a</span> = <span class="italic">b</span> = 8.85431 , <span class="italic">c</span> = 21.68460 , and <span class="italic">V</span> = 1472.285  (Table S2<a title="Select to navigate to footnote" href="#fn1"></a>). Furthermore, the fitness of the plot (inset in <a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig1">Fig. 1c</a>) verifies the validity of the refinement process.</p>
      <p class="otherpara">The detailed microstructures of the pyro-synthesized NMVTP/C were observed through FE-SEM (Fig. S5<a title="Select to navigate to footnote" href="#fn1"></a>) and HR-TEM (<a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig1">Fig. 1e</a>). NMVTP/C exhibits a flake-like morphology with sizes ranging from 100500 nm (Fig. S5a and b<a title="Select to navigate to footnote" href="#fn1"></a>). Whereas the NMVAP/C and NMVFP/C cathodes exhibit microparticle-like morphology Fig. S5c and d.<a title="Select to navigate to footnote" href="#fn1"></a> The amorphous carbon layer with a thickness of 5 nm on the surface of the NMVTP/C microflakes is observed in <a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig1">Fig. 1f</a>. The high-resolution TEM image of the single flakes in <a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig1">Fig. 1g</a> exhibits highly crystalline lattice fringes with an interplanar spacing of 0.61 nm, which is attributed to the (012) plane of the trigonal crystal system, as previously indicated by the PXRD pattern. The TEM/energy dispersive X-ray mapping study reveals the consistent presence of Na, Mn, V, Ti, P, O, and C in the selected area in <a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig1">Fig. 1h</a>, further confirming the purity of the sample. Thermogravimetric analysis (TGA) was carried out on NMVTP/C to determine the precise C content; the corresponding TGA plot is shown in Fig. S6a.<a title="Select to navigate to footnote" href="#fn1"></a> The amount of C in the NMVTP/C material was found to be 4.73%. Raman spectroscopy was carried out to elucidate the nature of the C shielded on the NMVTP/C material, and the corresponding results are given in Fig. S6b.<a title="Select to navigate to footnote" href="#fn1"></a> The Raman spectrum comprises two characteristic peaks at 1349.71 cm<small><sup>1</sup></small> (D-band) and 1592.84 cm<small><sup>1</sup></small>(G-band). The ratio of sp<small><sup>3</sup></small> to sp<small><sup>2</sup></small> (<span class="italic">i.e.</span>, the ratio of <span class="italic">I</span><small><sub>D</sub></small>/<span class="italic">I</span><small><sub>G</sub></small>) is determined to be 0.85, indicating that the C in the sample is amorphous in nature.<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit38"><sup><span class="sup_ref">38</span></sup></a> Likewise, the ratio of <span class="italic">I</span><small><sub>D</sub></small>/<span class="italic">I</span><small><sub>G</sub></small> is determined to be 0.84 and 0.85 for NMVFP/C and NMVAP/C cathodes, respectively; indicating that the carbon features are amorphous as that of the NMVTP/C cathode in Fig. S6b.<a title="Select to navigate to footnote" href="#fn1"></a> Additionally, XPS was employed to identify the chemical composition and oxidation state of the transition metals in the NMVTP/C samples. The V 2p profile in Fig. S7a<a title="Select to navigate to footnote" href="#fn1"></a> exhibits two major peaks with binding energies of 519.2 and 522.8 eV, corresponding to the 2p<small><sub>3/2</sub></small> and 2p<small><sub>1/2</sub></small> spinorbit energy phase, respectively, with a separation of 3.6 eV. This is ascribed to the trivalent nature of V in the NMVTP/C sample.<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit39"><sup><span class="sup_ref">39</span></sup></a> The Mn 2p profile in Fig. S7b<a title="Select to navigate to footnote" href="#fn1"></a> displays peaks at 642.3 and 653.4 eV, corresponding to 2p<small><sub>3/2</sub></small> and 2p<small><sub>1/2</sub></small>, respectively, with spinorbit splitting energy of 11.1 eV. This indicates that the binding energy of Mn is 2+.<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit40"><sup><span class="sup_ref">40</span></sup></a> Moreover, the paramagnetic metal phase appears at 645.9 and 656.6 eV in the form of shake-up satellites.<a title="Select to navigate to reference" href="#cit41"><sup><span class="sup_ref">41,42</span></sup></a> The Ti 2p XPS profile in Fig. S8a<a title="Select to navigate to footnote" href="#fn1"></a> exhibits peaks at 459.4 and 464.9 eV, with an energy separation of 5.5 eV; this points to the tetravalent nature of Ti<small><sup>4+</sup></small>.<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit43"><sup><span class="sup_ref">43</span></sup></a> The C 1s XPS profile in Fig. S8b<a title="Select to navigate to footnote" href="#fn1"></a> reveals two main peaks at 284.6 and 285.2 eV, corresponding to sp<small><sup>2</sup></small> graphitized and sp<small><sup>3</sup></small> diamond-like carbon CC units, respectively.<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit44"><sup><span class="sup_ref">44</span></sup></a> The small peak at 289.1 eV signifies COO bonds condensed on the surface.<a title="Select to navigate to reference" href="#cit45"><sup><span class="sup_ref">45,46</span></sup></a> The O 1s XPS profile in Fig. S8c<a title="Select to navigate to footnote" href="#fn1"></a> displays peaks at 530.9, 532.4, and 535.3 eV, attributed to MO, COC, and COO bonds, respectively.<a title="Select to navigate to reference" href="#cit47"><sup><span class="sup_ref">47,48</span></sup></a> The Na 1s and P 2p XPS profiles in Fig. S8d and S8e<a title="Select to navigate to footnote" href="#fn1"></a> reveal a pronounced peak at 1071.5 eV and 133.1 eV, respectively, signifying the existence of Na and P in the sample. Summing up these observations, the survey spectrum in Fig. S8f<a title="Select to navigate to footnote" href="#fn1"></a> indicates the purity of the NMVTP/C sample.</p>
      <p class="otherpara">Electrochemical sodium storage properties of three cathodes are studied using the CV technique in a half cell at a sweep rate of 0.1 mV s<small><sup>1</sup></small> in the voltage domain between 4.151.5 V. The resultant CV profiles of the NMVAP/C, NMVFP/C, and NMVTP/C cathodes are illustrated in <a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig2">Fig. 2ac</a>. From CV profiles of NMVAP/C, there are three curves (V<small><sup>3+/4+</sup></small> (3.5 V), Mn<small><sup>2+/3+</sup></small> (3.7 V), and V<small><sup>4+/5+</sup></small> (4.05 V)) existed during the positive scan, validating the involvement of V and Mn in the extraction of Na<small><sup>+</sup></small> from the NMVAP/C structure. A similar phenomenon has been observed in earlier studies, which reported that the incorporation of Al<small><sup>3+</sup></small> induces the high-valence redox activity of V.<a title="Select to navigate to reference" href="#cit14"><sup><span class="sup_ref">14,49</span></sup></a> Nevertheless, the disappearance of Mn<small><sup>2+/3+</sup></small> in the subsequent cycle specifies the poor electrochemical reversibility associated with structural failure. It is worth noting that the NMVFP/C and NMVTP/C cathodes reveal V<small><sup>4+/5+</sup></small> (4.05 V) redox couples along with the V<small><sup>2+/3+</sup></small> (1.6 V) redox couples. Yet these sample doesn't exhibit specific peaks for Mn<small><sup>2+/3+</sup></small> and V<small><sup>3+/4+</sup></small>, rather a single peak is observed at 3.58 V and 3.6 V for NMVFP/C and NMVTP/C, respectively. This could be associated with the composition of Mn<small><sup>2+/3+</sup></small> and V<small><sup>3+/4+</sup></small> due to their small voltage difference as evidenced in the earlier reports.<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit50"><sup><span class="sup_ref">50</span></sup></a> In addition, the Fe<small><sup>2+/3+</sup></small> (3.1 V) and Ti<small><sup>3+/4+</sup></small> (2.2 V) redox couples are witnessed for NMVFP/C and NMVTP/C, respectively.<a title="Select to navigate to reference" href="#cit51"><sup><span class="sup_ref">51,52</span></sup></a></p>
      <br><div class="image_table"><table><tbody><tr><td colspan="3" class="imgHolder" id="imgfig2"><a href="/image/article/2023/TA/d3ta02291a/d3ta02291a-f2_hi-res.gif" title="Select to open image in new window" onclick="open(this.href, &quot;_blank&quot;, &quot;toolbar=1,scrollbars=yes,resizable=1&quot;); return false;"><img alt="image file: d3ta02291a-f2.tif" src="/image/article/2023/TA/d3ta02291a/d3ta02291a-f2.gif"></a></td></tr><tr><td class="pushTitleRight"> </td><td class="image_title"><b>Fig. 2 </b> <span id="fig2"><span class="graphic_title">CV profile at 0.1 mV s<small><sup>1</sup></small> for (a) NMVAP/C, (b) NMVFP/C, and (c) NMVTP/C cathodes. Rate performance acquired at various C rates for (d) NMVAP/C, (e) NMVFP/C, and (f) NMVTP/C cathodes. Charge/discharge pattern at 0.17C for (g) NMVAP/C, (h) NMVFP/C, and (i) NMVTP/C cathodes.</span></span></td><td class="pushTitleLeft"> </td></tr></tbody></table></div>
      <p class="otherpara">The rate performance output is provided in (<a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig2">Fig. 2df</a>), with an increase of C-rates, the NMVTP/C cathode exhibits superior rate stability followed by the NMVFP/C cathode. Notably, the NMVAP/C experienced a rapid capacity decay with an increase in C-rates. The NMVAP/C, NMVFP/C, and NMVTP/C cathodes could register capacities of 82, 113.4, and 133.14 mA h g<small><sup>1</sup></small> at 0.17C, respectively. The reversible capacity achieved by NMVTP/C (59.2 mA h g<small><sup>1</sup></small>) cathode at a 17.5C rate is far ahead of NMVAP/C (10 mA h g<small><sup>1</sup></small>), and NMVFP/C (31 mA h g<small><sup>1</sup></small>) cathodes. The electrochemical properties (charge/discharge profiles) of the three cathodes in the voltage region of 4.151.5 V at 0.17C rate for the first two cycles are presented in (<a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig2">Fig. 2gi</a>). The voltage plateau and redox couple position of the three samples is in line with the CV observation. Furthermore, to visualize the stability features of these electrodes, electrochemical impedance spectroscopy (EIS) studies were performed before and after the cycling process. The resultant Nyquist plots of all samples are shown in Fig. S9ac.<a title="Select to navigate to footnote" href="#fn1"></a> The respective Nyquist plots were fitted utilizing the electrochemical equivalent circuit (inset in Fig. S9ac<a title="Select to navigate to footnote" href="#fn1"></a>). The fitting constraints for the NMVAP/C, NMVFP/C, and NMVTP/C are provided in Table S3, S4, and S5,<a title="Select to navigate to footnote" href="#fn1"></a> respectively. Where, R1, R2, R3, R4, Q1, Q3, Q4, and W have represented the solution or electrolyte resistance (<span class="italic">R</span>s), the resistance of the solid electrolyte interface (<span class="italic">R</span><small><sub>SEI</sub></small>), solid electrolyte interface capacitance (<span class="italic">Q</span><small><sub>SEI</sub></small> or <span class="italic">C</span><small><sub>SEI</sub></small>), charge transfer resistance (<span class="italic">R</span><small><sub>CT</sub></small>), the capacitance of charge transfer (<span class="italic">Q</span><small><sub>CT</sub></small> or <span class="italic">C</span><small><sub>CT</sub></small>), and Warburg elements diffusion resistance, respectively.<a title="Select to navigate to reference" href="#cit53"><sup><span class="sup_ref">5355</span></sup></a> The corresponding resistance outputs of the different cathodes before and after cycling process is compared in the Fig S10.<a title="Select to navigate to footnote" href="#fn1"></a> It is evident that the <span class="italic">R</span><small><sub>s</sub></small> and <span class="italic">R</span><small><sub>SEI</sub></small> have a minimal contribution to the internal resistance of the respective cathodes investigated in this investigation. On the other hand, before cycling process, the calculated charge transfer resistance (<span class="italic">R</span><small><sub>CT</sub></small>) values had a major contribution to the overall resistance of the different cathodes analysed here. In specific, <span class="italic">R</span><small><sub>CT</sub></small> values of NMVAP/C, NMVFP/C, and NMVTP/C are 1592, 1145, and 913.6 , respectively. After-cycling process overall <span class="italic">R</span><small><sub>CT</sub></small> values of NMVAP/C, NMVFP/C, and NMVTP/C are decreased (1025, 485.8, and 280.7 ) indicating a low charge transfer capability compared to the before-cycle samples. Overall, the NMVTP/C sample exhibited less resistance than the NMVFP/C and NMVAP/C, which is in line with the galvanostatic and rate performance outputs. Thus, the combined electrochemical studies (galvanostatic study, rate output, and EIS) substantiate our ML-DFT-assisted predictions <span class="italic">i.e.</span>, the NMVTP/C has superior crystal stability, which ensures good electrochemical stability.</p>
      <p class="otherpara">From the charge/discharge output of the NMVTP/C, we have calculated the number of moles of Na<small><sup>+</sup></small> that participated during the electrochemical process (<a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig2">Fig. 2i</a>). In specific, the charge profile exhibits an extraction capacity of 128.56 mA h g<small><sup>1</sup></small> with two strong plateaus at 3.4 and 3.8 V. This indicates the two-step extraction of 2.25 moles Na<small><sup>+</sup></small> ions from the NMVTP cathode <span class="italic">i.e.</span>, the formation of Na<small><sub>1.25</sub></small>MnV<small><sub>0.5</sub></small>Ti<small><sub>0.5</sub></small>(PO<small><sub>4</sub></small>)<small><sub>3</sub></small> (N<small><sub>1.25</sub></small>MVTP) phase with respect to the oxidation of V<small><sup>3+</sup></small>V<small><sup>4+</sup></small>, Mn<small><sup>2+</sup></small>  Mn<small><sup>3+</sup></small>, and V<small><sup>4+</sup></small>  V<small><sup>5+</sup></small>. Meanwhile, the discharge curve displays a discharge capacity of 133.14 mA h g<small><sup>1</sup></small> with two principal voltage plateaus at 3.98 and 3.48 V, suggesting the insertion of 2.33 moles of Na<small><sup>+</sup></small> ions into the NMVTP/C structure regulated by the reduction of V<small><sup>5+</sup></small>  V<small><sup>4+</sup></small>, Mn<small><sup>3+</sup></small>  Mn<small><sup>2+</sup></small>, and V<small><sup>4+</sup></small>  V<small><sup>3+</sup></small>. More importantly, the inclusion of Ti provided additional insertion pathways at 2.25 V (driven by the reduction of Ti<small><sup>4+</sup></small>  Ti<small><sup>3+</sup></small>) and 1.6 V (driven by the reduction of V<small><sup>2+</sup></small>  V<small><sup>3+</sup></small>) for the Na<small><sup>+</sup></small> ions to achieve Na<small><sub>3.58</sub></small>MnV<small><sub>0.5</sub></small>Ti<small><sub>0.5</sub></small>(PO<small><sub>4</sub></small>)<small><sub>3</sub></small> (N<small><sub>3.58</sub></small>MVTP) phase (the average Na<small><sup>+</sup></small> (de)insertion voltage is retained at 3.42 V). The continuous Na<small><sup>+</sup></small> (de)insertion properties of the NMVTP/C cathode were monitored for 300 cycles at a rate of 0.77C in the potential range of 4.151.5 V; the resultant cycling stability curve is provided in <a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig3">Fig. 3a</a>. After supplying 112 mA h g<small><sup>1</sup></small> at the first cycle the NMVTP/C cathode can retain a reversible capacity of 94 mA h g<small><sup>1</sup></small> following 300 cycles, with a capacity retention of 83%, and maintains a coulombic efficiency of almost 100%. This demonstrates the excellent sodium storage property of the NASICON-type NMVTP/C cathode even after repeated charge/discharge cycles, owing to its inherent structural stability. Selected charge/discharge patterns (after 100, 200, and 300 cycles) for the NMVTP/C cathode at a current density of 0.77C are provided in Fig. S11a.<a title="Select to navigate to footnote" href="#fn1"></a>The voltage plateaus are maintained in successive cycles, indicating that the Na<small><sup>+</sup></small> (de)insertion into the NMVTP/C structure follows the same pathway.</p>
      <br><div class="image_table"><table><tbody><tr><td colspan="3" class="imgHolder" id="imgfig3"><a href="/image/article/2023/TA/d3ta02291a/d3ta02291a-f3_hi-res.gif" title="Select to open image in new window" onclick="open(this.href, &quot;_blank&quot;, &quot;toolbar=1,scrollbars=yes,resizable=1&quot;); return false;"><img alt="image file: d3ta02291a-f3.tif" src="/image/article/2023/TA/d3ta02291a/d3ta02291a-f3.gif"></a></td></tr><tr><td class="pushTitleRight"> </td><td class="image_title"><b>Fig. 3 </b> <span id="fig3"><span class="graphic_title">(a) Cyclability pattern acquired at 0.77C. Cyclability curve at (b) 10.5C and (c) 14C, respectively. (d) Ragone-plot of NMVTP/C cathode along with that of different polyanion electrodes available in the literature.</span></span></td><td class="pushTitleLeft"> </td></tr></tbody></table></div>
      <p class="otherpara">Moreover, the stable voltage profile in the charge/discharge curves suggests that the redox features of V<small><sup>2+/3+</sup></small>, Ti<small><sup>3+/4+</sup></small>, V<small><sup>3+/4+</sup></small>, Mn<small><sup>2+/3+</sup></small>, and V<small><sup>4+/5+</sup></small> in the NMVTP/C are preserved throughout the cycles. Likewise, the voltage shapes are retained at the different current densities in the voltage range of 4.151.5 V (Fig. S11b<a title="Select to navigate to footnote" href="#fn1"></a>), further confirming the structural integrity and electrochemical Na reversibility of the NMVTP/C cathode both of which are vital benchmarks for any cathode material. The superior rate performance at all current densities in the wide voltage range demonstrates the electrochemical stability of the NMVTP/C cathode, which most SIB electrode materials do not exhibit. The rapid Na<small><sup>+</sup></small> (de)insertion capability of the NMVTP/C cathode was also evaluated at a current rate of 10.5C and 14C in the voltage range of 4.151.5 V for prolonged cycles; the resultant cycling performances are presented in <a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig3">Fig. 3b and c</a>.</p>
      <p class="otherpara">After delivering a maximum discharge capacity of 92 and 84 mA h g<small><sup>1</sup></small> at a rate of 10.5C and 14C, reversible capacities of 70 and 63 mA h g<small><sup>1</sup></small> are maintained after 1500 and 8000 cycles, respectively. This implies that at rates of 10.5C and 14C, the prevalent capacity retentions are 76% and 75%, respectively are retained. More importantly, the corresponding selected charge/discharge patterns at the respective rates, as shown in Fig. S11c and S11d,<a title="Select to navigate to footnote" href="#fn1"></a> preserve their shape and redox peak position throughout prolonged cycling, indicating the rapid and stable egress/ingress of Na<small><sup>+</sup></small> ions from/into the NMVTP/C skeleton without sacrificing the redox properties. To recognize the importance of structural stability of the NMVTP/C during frequent Na<small><sup>+</sup></small> insertion/extraction processes, the ex situ XRD analysis was performed after the cycling process. The cells at 17C after long-term cycles were disassembled and subjected to XRD analysis. From the Fig. S12,<a title="Select to navigate to footnote" href="#fn1"></a> it is obvious that the XRD patterns of the NMVTP/C cathode are largely preserved, which is crucial in assisting the Na<small><sup>+</sup></small> insertion/extraction process for the most part of the cycling process. Yet, an in-depth understanding of the structural and valence state changes associated with the transition metal ions during the charge/discharge process of the NMVTP/C cathode using advanced characterization practices could be essential, which will be focused in future studies.<a title="Select to navigate to reference" href="#cit56"><sup><span class="sup_ref">5659</span></sup></a> It must be noted that an exceedingly small number of cathode materials for SIBs have been demonstrated to display stable voltage curves at rapid testing rates. As summarized in the Ragone plot (<a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig3">Fig. 3d</a>), the NMVTP/C cathode exhibits the best performance among the polyanion-based sodium cathodes compared in this study.<a title="Select to navigate to reference" href="#cit7"><sup><span class="sup_ref">7,1517,50,6065</span></sup></a> In particular, NMVTP/C exhibits the highest specific energy of 455 W h kg<small><sup>1</sup></small> at a specific power of 85.5 W kg<small><sup>1</sup></small> (based on the mass of the cathode material). Moreover, the electrochemical performance of the NMVAP/C, NMVFP/C, and NMVTP/C cathode is compared with previously reported NASICON-type cathodes in Table S6.<a title="Select to navigate to footnote" href="#fn1"></a> In specific, NMVTP/C cathode holds superior electrochemical properties than the compared cathodes highlighting the advantages of combination of Mn, V, and Ti elements in the NASICON structure.</p>
      <p class="otherpara">The electrochemical kinetics of the NMVTP/C cathode was further investigated by performing CV at distinct voltage sweep domains from 0.1 to 0.5 mV s<small><sup>1</sup></small>, and the outcomes are presented in <a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig4">Fig. 4a</a>. As the sweep rate increases from 0.1 to 0.5 mV s<small><sup>1</sup></small>, the peaks in the CV patterns are progressively amplified. At a particular potential, the contribution of diffusion-limited reaction kinetics and capacitance kinetics can be determined quantitatively from the following equation:<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit66"><sup><span class="sup_ref">66</span></sup></a></p><table><tbody><tr><td class="leftEqn">&nbsp;</td></tr><tr><td class="eqn"><span id="eqn1"><span id="eqn1"><span class="italic">i</span> = <span class="italic">k</span><small><sub>1</sub></small><span class="italic">v</span> + <span class="italic">k</span><small><sub>2</sub></small><span class="italic">v</span><small><sup>1/2</sup></small>,</span></span></td><td class="rightEqn">(1)</td></tr></tbody></table>where <span class="italic">k</span><small><sub>1</sub></small><span class="italic">v</span> refers to the surface capacitance process, and <span class="italic">k</span><small><sub>2</sub></small><span class="italic">v</span><small><sup>1/2</sup></small> refers to the diffusion-driven redox reaction at a definite scan rate.<a title="Select to navigate to reference" href="#cit37"><sup><span class="sup_ref">37,67</span></sup></a> The surface capacitance-consumption data at all examined voltages were calculated and plotted in <a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig4">Fig. 4b</a>. At a rate of 0.1 mV s<small><sup>1</sup></small>, the calculated surface capacitance (shaded region) corresponds to 29.25% of the total capacity. <a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig4">Fig. 4c</a> presents the histogram of the capacitive and diffusion-driven consumption at progressive scan rates. The surface-induced reaction dominates at higher scan rates. Interestingly, even at a high scan rate (0.5 mV s<small><sup>1</sup></small>), more than 35.3% of the redox reaction takes place through the diffusion-induced intercalation process. This demonstrates that the capacity of the cathode mainly originates from the diffusion-driven Na<small><sup>+</sup></small> (de)intercalation process. The Na migration kinetics and phase transition of the NASICON-type NMVTP/C cathode were observed by performing GITT at 0.15C with 10 min intervals between each pulse. The cathode was rested for 2 h to obtain a quasi-equilibrium potential, and it was examined under the potential range of 4.151.5 V. The resultant titration curve for the first cycle is presented in <a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig4">Fig. 4d</a>.<p></p>
      <br><div class="image_table"><table><tbody><tr><td colspan="3" class="imgHolder" id="imgfig4"><a href="/image/article/2023/TA/d3ta02291a/d3ta02291a-f4_hi-res.gif" title="Select to open image in new window" onclick="open(this.href, &quot;_blank&quot;, &quot;toolbar=1,scrollbars=yes,resizable=1&quot;); return false;"><img alt="image file: d3ta02291a-f4.tif" src="/image/article/2023/TA/d3ta02291a/d3ta02291a-f4.gif"></a></td></tr><tr><td class="pushTitleRight"> </td><td class="image_title"><b>Fig. 4 </b> <span id="fig4"><span class="graphic_title">(a) Multi-scan CV profile at various scan rates. (b) The contribution ratio of the diffusion-limited capacities and capacitive capacities at 0.1 mV s<small><sup>1</sup></small>. (c) Bar chart for capacity contribution ratios at different scan rates. GITT analysis of NMVTP/C cathode. (d) Voltage profile during GITT at 20 mA g<small><sup>1</sup></small> current density, sodium ion chemical diffusion coefficient calculated from GITT curves during the electrochemical Na<small><sup>+</sup></small> (de)insertion process (<span class="italic">i.e.</span>) (e) charge and (f) Discharge, respectively.</span></span></td><td class="pushTitleLeft"> </td></tr></tbody></table></div>
      <p class="otherpara">The sodium diffusion coefficient can be calculated from the transient voltage established in the GITT curves and using Fick's second law:<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit68"><sup><span class="sup_ref">68</span></sup></a></p><table><tbody><tr><td class="leftEqn">&nbsp;</td></tr><tr><td class="eqn"><span id="eqn2"><span id="eqn2"><span class="italic">D</span><small><sub>Na</sub></small> = 4/<span class="italic"></span>(<span class="italic">m</span><small><sub>B</sub></small><span class="italic">V</span><small><sub>M</sub></small>/<span class="italic">M</span><small><sub>w</sub></small><span class="italic">A</span>)<small><sup>2</sup></small>(<span class="italic">E</span><small><sub>s</sub></small>/<span class="italic">E</span><small><sub></sub></small>)<small><sup>2</sup></small>,</span></span></td><td class="rightEqn">(2)</td></tr></tbody></table>where <span class="italic">D</span><small><sub>Na</sub></small> is the sodium chemical diffusion coefficient (cm<small><sup>2</sup></small> s<small><sup>1</sup></small>) and <span class="italic">m</span><small><sub>B,</sub></small><span class="italic">V</span><small><sub>M</sub></small>, <span class="italic">M</span><small><sub>W</sub></small>, and <span class="italic">A</span> are the mass loading (g), molar volume (cm<small><sup>3</sup></small> mol<small><sup>1</sup></small>), molecular weight (g mol<small><sup>1</sup></small>), and sum of the surface area (cm<small><sup>2</sup></small>) of the NMVTP/C cathode, respectively. <span class="italic"></span> (s) is the time of the applied current pulse, and <span class="italic">E</span><small><sub>s</sub></small> and <span class="italic">E</span><small><sub></sub></small> are the variations in the steady-state voltage and total difference in the cell voltage arising from the persistent pulse of a single-stage GITT investigation, respectively. The continuous variation in the equilibrium voltage indicates the single-phase reaction mechanism for the Na<small><sup>+</sup></small> (de)intercalation between 4.15 and 1.5 V (<a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig4">Fig. 4d</a>). The corresponding diffusion coefficient for the charge and discharge processes are plotted in <a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig4">Fig. 4e and f</a>. The calculated diffusion coefficients are in the ranges of 2.25  10<small><sup>8</sup></small> to 9.51  10<small><sup>9</sup></small> and 5.26  10<small><sup>8</sup></small> to 9.71  10<small><sup>9</sup></small> for the extraction and de-intercalation processes, respectively. This signifies the rapid Na<small><sup>+</sup></small> flow in the NMVTP/C cathode.<a title="Select to navigate to reference" href="#cit37"><sup><span class="sup_ref">37,68</span></sup></a> In particular, the rise and drop of the diffusion coefficient during the charge and discharge processes, respectively, around the voltage regions of 2.27/2.13, 3.62/3.36, and 3.9/3.8 V suggest that the Ti<small><sup>3+</sup></small>/Ti<small><sup>4+</sup></small>, V<small><sup>3+</sup></small>/V<small><sup>4+</sup></small>, Mn<small><sup>2+</sup></small>/Mn<small><sup>3+</sup></small>, and V<small><sup>4+</sup></small>/V<small><sup>5+</sup></small> redox activities induce the reversible Na<small><sup>+</sup></small> extraction and insertion in the NMVTP/C cathode. The enhanced Na<small><sup>+</sup></small> diffusivity contributes to the rapid sodium storage property of the NMVTP/C cathode, thus resulting in its excellent rate properties and rapid current exploration abilities.<p></p>
      <p class="otherpara">
        <span class="italic">In situ</span> XRD observations were carried out to determine the structural evolution of the NMVTP/C cathode during the Na<small><sup>+</sup></small> (de)insertion process. The designed cell was initially charged to 4.15 V and discharged to 1.5 V at a current density of 0.17C. The <span class="italic">in situ</span> 2D contour map profiles along with the equivalent charge/discharge schemes are presented in <a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig5">Fig. 5a</a>. The seven projected peaks for the uncharged electrode can be allocated as the (104), (113), (024), (211), (122), and (030) Bragg planes of the parent NMVTP/C cathode. The (006) plane alone exhibited practically no alterations during the charge and discharge conditions. Excitingly, as the Na<small><sup>+</sup></small> extraction commenced, the peaks corresponding to the (104), (113), (024), (211), (122), and (030) planes of NMVTP/C slightly moved toward a higher angle. This indicates that the initial sodium charging was induced by the V<small><sup>3+</sup></small>  V<small><sup>4+</sup></small> and Mn<small><sup>2+</sup></small>  Mn<small><sup>3+</sup></small> redox-dominated single-phase sodium extraction. However, it is interesting to witness that the (113), (024), (122), and (030) planes at 23.32, 28.24, 31.72, and 34.77, respectively disappeared, and new peaks evolved at 23.93, 28.92, 32.72, and 36.11, respectively, representing the two-phase reaction originating from the V<small><sup>4+</sup></small>  V<small><sup>5+</sup></small> transition. More interestingly, the new peaks at 23.93, 28.92, 32.72, and 36.11 uninterruptedly shifted to a higher 2<span class="italic"></span> angle, with no peak evolving further, indicating that solid-solution reaction has prevailed in the NMVTP/C cathode. Whereas (104) diffraction shape alone splits into two peaks that evolved sharply during the charge course. Thus, the appearance of new peaks and disappearance of the prevailing peaks during the charging process suggest that further Na<small><sup>+</sup></small> extraction was constrained by the bi-phasic transition stemming from the V<small><sup>4+</sup></small>  V<small><sup>5+</sup></small> redox species.<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit69"><sup><span class="sup_ref">69</span></sup></a> As the discharge process was initiated, all peaks began to return to their original states. Notably, after discharging, the (104) peak, which underwent splitting began to integrate into the original peak, as indicated by the open-circuit voltage (OCV). Furthermore, the new peaks at 23.93, 28.92, 32.72, and 36.11 shifted back to a lower 2<span class="italic"></span> angle and disappeared. And the peaks corresponding to the (113), (024), (122), and (030) planes reappear in their original position, signifying that the original framework is restored at the end of the first cycle. This strongly suggests that the reversible phase transition occurs between 4.15 and 1.5 V.<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit17"><sup><span class="sup_ref">17</span></sup></a></p>
      <br><div class="image_table"><table><tbody><tr><td colspan="3" class="imgHolder" id="imgfig5"><a href="/image/article/2023/TA/d3ta02291a/d3ta02291a-f5_hi-res.gif" title="Select to open image in new window" onclick="open(this.href, &quot;_blank&quot;, &quot;toolbar=1,scrollbars=yes,resizable=1&quot;); return false;"><img alt="image file: d3ta02291a-f5.tif" src="/image/article/2023/TA/d3ta02291a/d3ta02291a-f5.gif"></a></td></tr><tr><td class="pushTitleRight"> </td><td class="image_title"><b>Fig. 5 </b> <span id="fig5"><span class="graphic_title">Sodium storage properties of NMVTP/C cathode (a) the <span class="italic">in situ</span> 2D contour map profiles along with the equivalent charge/discharge schemes. (b) Lattice parameter and unit cell volume changes upon Na<small><sup>+</sup></small> (de)insertion.</span></span></td><td class="pushTitleLeft"> </td></tr></tbody></table></div>
      <p class="otherpara">Additionally, <span class="italic">in situ</span> XRD profile provides us with a firm sodium storage assessment (Fig. S13<a title="Select to navigate to footnote" href="#fn1"></a>), which offers a solid visualization of the structural changes in NMVTP/C cathode materials. In sum, all peaks underwent a considerable shift, following which they progressively returned to the original state, signifying that the charge/discharge process is highly reversible. The change in the peak positions indicates a single-phase solid-solution reaction, while the appearance of new peaks or the disappearance of existing ones indicates a biphasic reaction. Thus, the NMVTP/C cathode subsequently undergoes a reversible solid-solution and bi-phasic transition during the electrochemical Na<small><sup>+</sup></small> (de)insertion process, resulting in its well-established voltage configuration. To corroborate the findings from the <span class="italic">in situ</span> study regarding the sodium storage mechanism of the NMVTP/C cathode, <span class="italic">ex situ</span> XRD measurements were carried out. The <span class="italic">ex situ</span> XRD patterns at various charge/discharge depths exhibit equivalent patterns to that of the of <span class="italic">in situ</span> XRD observation (<span class="italic">i.e.</span> shift of the (113), (024), and (122) peaks, splitting/merging of the (104) peak, and appearance/disappearance of the (030) peak) (Fig. S14<a title="Select to navigate to footnote" href="#fn1"></a>). Thus, the correspondence between the results of the <span class="italic">in situ</span> and <span class="italic">ex situ</span> observations confirms the solid-solution and bi-phasic processes. In command to acquire a deep understanding of the volume variation upon Na<small><sup>+</sup></small> (de)intercalation courses, the Le Bail fitting is performed using the X'pert Highscore program. As interpreted in <a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig5">Fig. 5b</a>, the unit cell volume slowly shrinks during the de-insertion period and enlarges during the re-insertion process. The overall volume alteration (after charge/discharge period) is estimated to be around 4.7% (<span class="italic">V</span>/<span class="italic">V</span><small><sub>Parent</sub></small>) and is near to that of Na<small><sub>3</sub></small>V<small><sub>2</sub></small>(PO<small><sub>4</sub></small>)<small><sub>3</sub></small>, but is less than that of Na<small><sub>4</sub></small>MnV(PO<small><sub>4</sub></small>)<small><sub>3</sub></small>.<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit70"><sup><span class="sup_ref">70</span></sup></a> The considerably a smaller amount of volume variation is accountable for the superior rate performance of the present investigating NMVTP/C cathode.</p>
      <p class="otherpara">Based on these observations, the electrochemical mechanism arising in the NMVTP/C cathode during Na (de)insertion can be enlightened schematically in <a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig6">Fig. 6a</a>. The possible 2.25 moles of Na<small><sup>+</sup></small> extraction from the NMVTP cathode results in the formation of N<small><sub>1.25</sub></small>MVTP as an intermediate phase after the 1st charge (based capacity output at 0.17C). After the end of the 1st discharge process, N<small><sub>3.58</sub></small>MVTP is regained. To realize practical requests, we further demonstrate the Na ion full cells based on NMVTP/C cathode and hard carbon (HC) anode in the coin cell. The half-cell charge/discharge profile of NMVTP/C and HC anode is compared in Fig. S15a<a title="Select to navigate to footnote" href="#fn1"></a> for reference. HC anode is chemically pre-sodiated before cell assembly. The rate capability yield of the NMVTP/C//HC full-cell are 136, 126, 114, 102, and 100 mA h g<small><sup>1</sup></small> cycled at different rates of 0.07C, 0.14C, 0.28C, 0.56C, and 0.77C are superior (Fig. S15b<a title="Select to navigate to footnote" href="#fn1"></a>). Furthermore, the cycling stability of NMVTP/C//HC full-cell is tested for 100 cycles at 0.77C rate (initially the cathodes are run at 0.07C for better stability), which can retain a stable discharge capacity (74.5 mA h g<small><sup>1</sup></small>) with 78% capacity retention (<a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig6">Fig. 6b</a>), indicating the NMVTP/C//HC full-cell is comprehensive for real-world applications. The selected charge/discharge pattern validates the stable voltage platform and redox outputs of the NMVTP/C//HC full-cell for the most part of the cycling test (<a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig6">Fig. 6c</a>). The voltage <span class="italic">vs.</span> power density of plot NMVTP/C//HC is comparatively illustrated in <a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig6">Fig. 6d</a> with other sodium-full cell systems constructed using the pre-sodiation strategy available in the literature. Especially the energy density (347 W h kg<small><sup>1</sup></small> at 340 W kg<small><sup>1</sup></small> power density) of our NMVTP/C//HC full-cell significantly exceeds the performances of sodium-full devices namely, PC-Fe<small><sub>3</sub></small>O<small><sub>4</sub></small>//Na<small><sub>2</sub></small>FeP<small><sub>2</sub></small>O<small><sub>7</sub></small>,<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit71"><sup><span class="sup_ref">71</span></sup></a> SnC//Na<small><sub>3</sub></small>V<small><sub>2</sub></small>(PO<small><sub>4</sub></small>)<small><sub>3</sub></small>,<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit72"><sup><span class="sup_ref">72</span></sup></a> SbO-G//Na<small><sub>3</sub></small>V<small><sub>2</sub></small>(PO<small><sub>4</sub></small>)<small><sub>3</sub></small>,<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit73"><sup><span class="sup_ref">73</span></sup></a> Graphite//Na<small><sub>1.5</sub></small>VOPO<small><sub>4.8</sub></small>F<small><sub>0.7</sub></small>,<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit74"><sup><span class="sup_ref">74</span></sup></a> Na<small><sub>2</sub></small>Ti<small><sub>3</sub></small>O<small><sub>7</sub></small>//VOPO<small><sub>4</sub></small>,<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit75"><sup><span class="sup_ref">75</span></sup></a> NiO/Fe<small><sub>2</sub></small>O<small><sub>3</sub></small>//Na<small><sub>3</sub></small>V<small><sub>2</sub></small>(PO<small><sub>4</sub></small>)<small><sub>3</sub></small>.<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit76"><sup><span class="sup_ref">76</span></sup></a> CV profile of the NMVTP//HC full-cell at 0.1 mV s<small><sup>1</sup></small> reveals a well-established oxidation sites appear at 4.05, 3.5, and 1.63 V, and the reduction locations arise at 3.98, 3.33, and 1.93 V (Fig. S15c<a title="Select to navigate to footnote" href="#fn1"></a>). More importantly, the CV-tested full-cell is further subjected to power the digital appliances (charged again). Notably, the NMVTP/C//HC full-cell can retain a potential of 4.08 V (Fig. S15d<a title="Select to navigate to footnote" href="#fn1"></a>), which is very crucial in powering the LED light (Fig. S15e<a title="Select to navigate to footnote" href="#fn1"></a>) and electronic digital watch (Fig. S15f<a title="Select to navigate to footnote" href="#fn1"></a>). The NMVTP/C cathode material established in this work is recognized to be one of the finest electrochemical presentations and encouraging SIB systems, which could certainly be streamlined to large-scale constructions in near future. To further ensure the intrinsic role of the NMVTP cathode, Na migration paths, as well as its energy barrier were evaluated through bond valence site (BVS) energy calculation and the Na insertion voltage was predicted using DFT method.<a title="Select to navigate to reference" href="#cit77"><sup><span class="sup_ref">77,78</span></sup></a></p>
      <br><div class="image_table"><table><tbody><tr><td colspan="3" class="imgHolder" id="imgfig6"><a href="/image/article/2023/TA/d3ta02291a/d3ta02291a-f6_hi-res.gif" title="Select to open image in new window" onclick="open(this.href, &quot;_blank&quot;, &quot;toolbar=1,scrollbars=yes,resizable=1&quot;); return false;"><img alt="image file: d3ta02291a-f6.tif" src="/image/article/2023/TA/d3ta02291a/d3ta02291a-f6.gif"></a></td></tr><tr><td class="pushTitleRight"> </td><td class="image_title"><b>Fig. 6 </b> <span id="fig6"><span class="graphic_title">(a) Schematic illustration of the electrochemical Sodium storage properties of NMVTP cathode. (b) Cyclability profile and (c) selected charge/discharge pattern of the NMVTP/C//HC full-cell at 0.77C (d) voltage and energy density comparison.</span></span></td><td class="pushTitleLeft"> </td></tr></tbody></table></div>
      <p class="otherpara">We found that, as shown in <a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig7">Fig. 7a</a>, there are five possible pathways for Na<small><sup>+</sup></small> to migrate within the NMVTP, NMVAP, and NMVFP structures, represented in five different colors: P1, P2, P3, P4, and P5. It can be observed that Na ion in the NMVTP and NMVFP would likely diffuse through P1 pathway with corresponding energy barrier of 596 meV and 516 meV, respectively (<a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig7">Fig. 7bf</a>). In the other hand, the P5 pathway is likely more favorable for Na in NMVAP with the energy barrier of 516 meV. Generally, NMVTP has the lowest Na migration energy barrier inferring Na-storage superiority behavior than the other samples. For evaluating the phase stability upon Na insertion into NMVTP, the formation energy in various Na concentrations was calculated, and the corresponding convex hull was constructed. We screened 10 structures with the lowest electrostatic energy for each composition in Na<small><sub><span class="italic">x</span></sub></small>MnV<small><sub>0.5</sub></small>Ti<small><sub>0.5</sub></small>(PO<small><sub>4</sub></small>)<small><sub>3</sub></small> for <span class="italic">x</span> = 1, 1.5, 2, 2.5, 3, 3.5 and 4. As shown in <a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig7">Fig. 7g</a>, throughout all concentrations, it is found that there are 4 stable structures between Na<small><sub>1</sub></small>MnV<small><sub>0.5</sub></small>Ti<small><sub>0.5</sub></small>(PO<small><sub>4</sub></small>)<small><sub>3</sub></small> and Na<small><sub>4</sub></small>MnV<small><sub>0.5</sub></small>Ti<small><sub>0.5</sub></small>(PO<small><sub>4</sub></small>)<small><sub>3</sub></small>, <span class="italic">i.e.</span> Na<small><sub>1.5</sub></small>MnV<small><sub>0.5</sub></small>Ti<small><sub>0.5</sub></small>(PO<small><sub>4</sub></small>)<small><sub>3</sub></small>, Na<small><sub>2.5</sub></small>MnV<small><sub>0.5</sub></small>Ti<small><sub>0.5</sub></small>(PO<small><sub>4</sub></small>)<small><sub>3</sub></small>, and Na<small><sub>3.5</sub></small>MnV<small><sub>0.5</sub></small>Ti<small><sub>0.5</sub></small>(PO<small><sub>4</sub></small>)<small><sub>3</sub></small>. It can also be observed that some metastable phases can be reached electrochemically since they lie below the convex hull value of 0. The calculation also suggests the combination of two-phase and solid-solution reactions, as observed from experimental characterization. Based on the obtained convex hull, the theoretical insertion voltage was also developed (<a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig7">Fig. 7h</a>). The predicted Na insertion voltage is resemblance to that of electrochemical characterization. However, the subtle difference due to the low conductivity of the NASICON can be further improved using other carbon-based coating materials such as CNT or graphene. Overall, these theoretical studies are in good agreement with the experimental characterization and can be used for further materials large-scale development.</p>
      <br><div class="image_table"><table><tbody><tr><td colspan="3" class="imgHolder" id="imgfig7"><a href="/image/article/2023/TA/d3ta02291a/d3ta02291a-f7_hi-res.gif" title="Select to open image in new window" onclick="open(this.href, &quot;_blank&quot;, &quot;toolbar=1,scrollbars=yes,resizable=1&quot;); return false;"><img alt="image file: d3ta02291a-f7.tif" src="/image/article/2023/TA/d3ta02291a/d3ta02291a-f7.gif"></a></td></tr><tr><td class="pushTitleRight"> </td><td class="image_title"><b>Fig. 7 </b> <span id="fig7"><span class="graphic_title">(a) Possible Na<small><sup>+</sup></small> diffusion pathways in NMVTP, NMVAP, and NMVFP structures. P1, P2, P3, P4, and P5 pathways are represented by red, green, black, orange, and blue color, respectively. The migration energy barrier in the 5 different pathways: (b) Pathway 1, (c) Pathway 2, (d) Pathway 3, (e) Pathway 4, and (f) Pathway 5 of NMVTP, NMVAP, and NMVFP are represented by black, red, and blue color, respectively. (g) Formation energies and convex hull of NMVTP and (h) theoretical Na insertion voltage in NMVTP.</span></span></td><td class="pushTitleLeft"> </td></tr></tbody></table></div>
      <p class="otherpara">It must be emphasized here, as predicted from the ML-DFT model the NMVTP/C with the most stable formation energy demonstrated superior structural and electrochemical stabilities. Knowing that Fe and Al distribution in the earth's crust is ample, the realization of stable sodium storage properties from NMVAP/C and NMVFP/C cathodes could be highly beneficial. However, NMVAP/C and NMVFP/C cathodes with poor formation energy and large diffusion barrier exhibit insignificant sodium storage performance than the NMVTP/C with stable formation energy and low diffusion barrier. The interplay between the compositional and structural features might be effective to overcome these challenges, which needs further investigation.</p>
    
    
      
      <h2 id="sect903"><span class="a_heading">3. Conclusions</span></h2>
      <span>This study involved integrated ML model forecasts and DFT calculations to employ the valuable characteristics of low-cost and non-toxic elements (Al, Fe, and Ti) in formulating the new NASICON-type cathodes. The ML-DFT model predicted three NASICON-type cathodes, including NMVAP, NMVFP, and NMVTP for SIBs. Furthermore, both DFT and experimental outputs confirmed that the NMVTP/C cathode with a larger diffusion channel retains superior structural stability than the NMVAP/C and NMVFP/C cathodes fabricated for SIBs in this study. <span class="italic">In situ</span> XRD, <span class="italic">ex situ</span> XRD, and GITT analyses were employed to elucidate the electrochemical Na<small><sup>+</sup></small> (de)intercalation mechanism in the NMVTP/C cathode. The NMVTP/C//HC full cell can preserve an energy density of 347 W h kg<small><sup>1</sup></small> at a power density of 340 W kg<small><sup>1</sup></small>, indicating the suitability of the NMVTP/C cathode for SIBs. Therefore, our results are expected to promote the use of the NASICON-type NMVTP/C cathode as a typical cathode material for SIBs in the near future.</span>
